The elders who had accompanied Dhanya up the mountain came back down, carrying his robes, his alms-bowl, his water-pot, and his cloth-strainer, and presented them to Mahavira as the formal report of his death. The body has been left on the mountain; the implements come back. The transition from monk-on-earth to god-in-Sarvarthasiddha is now complete, recorded both in heaven by his arrival and on earth by the empty implements.

The Gujarati commentary closes with a powerful framing: "the seeker's life is the message of moment-to-moment vigilance; even in the most disciplined life there will be subtle lapses, and the final practice — *antima ārādhana* — is the moment when those lapses are confessed, the chain of fault is broken before it can carry into the next birth, and the soul departs in pure equanimity. This is why the highest grade of dying matters; it is the seal on every prior moment of practice."

**6. SIMPLY PUT**

In the late-night quiet, Dhanya realized his body was failing and decided to make this his final practice — he asked Mahavira's permission, climbed the great Vipula mountain with the elder monks, fasted in stillness for one month, and at the end of his nine-month monastic life he died in perfect calm and was reborn in Sarvarthasiddha, the very highest heaven of the Jain cosmos.

**7. CONTEMPLATE**

When the body you live in finally cannot serve the soul any longer — will you have prepared the soul to leave it cleanly, or will you spend that hour clutching at what is already gone?

---

### Dhanya's Future Liberation

### SUTRA 3.A1.S28 — Gautama's Question and the Prophecy of Mahavideha Liberation

**1. PRAKRIT TEXT**

भंते ! त्ति भगवं गोयमे तहेव आपुच्छइ जहा खंदयस्स । भगवं वागरेइ जाव सव्वट्टुसिद्धे विमाणे उववण्णे ।

धण्णस्स णं भंते ! देवस्स केवइयं कालं ठिई पण्णत्ता ?

गोयमा ! तेत्तीसं सागरोवमाइं ठिई पण्णत्ता ।

से णं भंते ! ताओ देवलोगाओ कहिं गच्छिहिइ ? कहिं उववज्जिहिइ ?

गोयमा ! महाविदेहे वासे सिज्झिहिइ । ॥3.A1.S28॥

**2. ROMAN TRANSLITERATION**

bhaṃte ! tti bhagavaṃ goyame taheva āpucchai jahā khaṃdayassa | bhagavaṃ vāgarei jāva savvaṭṭhasiddhe vimāṇe uvavaṇṇe |

dhaṇṇassa ṇaṃ bhaṃte ! devassa kevaiyaṃ kālaṃ ṭhiī paṇṇattā ?

goyamā ! tettīsaṃ sāgarovamāiṃ ṭhiī paṇṇattā |

se ṇaṃ bhaṃte ! tāo devalogāo kahiṃ gacchihii ? kahiṃ uvavajjihii ?

goyamā ! mahāvidehe vāse sijjhihii | || 3.A1.S28 ||

**3. LITERAL ENGLISH TRANSLATION**

"Reverend Sir!" — saying this, the venerable Gautama asked just as he had asked about Skandaka, and the Lord answered, up to "[Dhanya] was reborn in the Sarvarthasiddha celestial mansion." — "Reverend Sir! For how long is the lifespan of the divine Dhanya declared to be?" — "Gautama! His lifespan is declared to be thirty-three sāgaropamas." — "Reverend Sir! When that god of his falls from that heavenly realm, where will he go? Where will he be reborn?" — "Gautama! In the region of Mahavideha he will attain liberation."

**4. ANVAYARTHA**

*bhaṃte tti* = "O Reverend Sir" — the standard address | *bhagavaṃ goyame* = the venerable Gautama (Indrabhuti, the chief disciple) | *taheva āpucchai jahā khaṃdayassa* = he asks just as he had asked concerning Skandaka (in Bhagavati Sutra) | *bhagavaṃ vāgarei* = the Lord answers | *jāva savvaṭṭhasiddhe vimāṇe uvavaṇṇe* = up to "(he was) reborn in the Sarvarthasiddha celestial mansion" | *dhaṇṇassa ṇaṃ deva­ssa* = of the divine Dhanya (now a god) | *kevaiyaṃ kālaṃ ṭhiī paṇṇattā* = how long has the lifespan been declared? | *tettīsaṃ sāgarovamāiṃ* = thirty-three *sāgaropamas* (a vast cosmological time-unit; literally "ocean-similes," each *sāgaropama* being itself measured in unimaginably long subdivisions) | *ṭhiī paṇṇattā* = the lifespan has been declared | *tāo devalogāo* = from that heavenly realm | *kahiṃ gacchihii* = where will (the soul) go? | *kahiṃ uvavajjihii* = where will it be reborn? | *mahāvidehe vāse* = in the Mahavideha region (the karma-bhumi where Tirthankaras are eternally present) | *sijjhihii* = he will attain liberation, become a Siddha (literally "the accomplished one")

**5. COMMENTARY**

This sutra completes the spiritual arc of Dhanya's soul. Gautama Swami — Mahavira's chief disciple — steps forward as the questioner. The text tells us that he asks "just as he had asked about Skandaka" — a cross-reference to a famous exchange in the Bhagavati Sutra, where Gautama had asked Mahavira about the destiny of the monk Skandaka after his sallekhana. The questioning formula is established and reused; it is the canonical method for asking about a soul's afterlife and its eventual liberation.

Three pieces of information are given here: the *station* (Sarvarthasiddha), the *duration* (thirty-three *sāgaropamas*), and the *destination* (Mahavideha, where liberation will occur).

The duration — *tettīsaṃ sāgarovamāiṃ* — is the maximum lifespan possible in any embodied state in the entire Jain cosmos. *Sāgaropama* literally means "ocean-comparable," and it is an unimaginably long time-unit; thirty-three of them is the lifespan of the gods in Sarvarthasiddha, and no celestial or human can live longer. Dhanya's soul will dwell in that perfect station for that maximal span — neither weighed down by the lower karmas that pull souls back into the cycle of births, nor able to rise out of embodiment until that residual karma is exhausted by the slow erosion of celestial existence.

When that span ends and his celestial body falls away, his soul will be reborn — by the doctrine of Sarvarthasiddha — only and exactly in *Mahāvideha*. Mahavideha is one of the three karma-bhūmi continents of the Jain cosmos (the others being Bharata and Airavata), and it is unique because Tirthankaras are eternally present there: in any moment of cosmic time, somewhere in the eight regions of Mahavideha, a Tirthankara is teaching. This means that a soul born there has uninterrupted access to the highest teaching, and therefore — provided the soul is ripe — has every condition for liberation. Souls reborn from Sarvarthasiddha are by definition ripe; they will hear the teaching, undertake the practice, and reach liberation in that very Mahavideha birth. This is what *sijjhihii* — "he will attain Siddha-hood, he will be liberated" — means.

The grammatical force of *sijjhihii* is worth noting. It is in the future definite — not "may attain" or "is likely to attain," but *he will*. The Tirthankara's word here is a prophecy backed by direct knowing. There is no probabilistic margin; Dhanya's liberation is sealed.

This is the doctrinal payoff of the entire chapter. From the very beginning — from the moment in part A when Dhanya was born to Bhadra Sarthavahi and described as supremely auspicious — every detail has been pointing here. The wealth, the royal marriages, the awakening at Mahavira's discourse, the renunciation, the four severe vows, the daily one-alms-piece practice, the wasted body radiant under its ash, Mahavira's verdict, Shrenika's veneration, the night-vigil reflection, the sallekhana on Vipula mountain, the ascent past every realm to Sarvarthasiddha — all of it converges on this single line: *mahāvidehe vāse sijjhihii*. He will be liberated.

The Gujarati commentary adds: this is the canonical demonstration that the path of right faith, right knowledge, and right conduct, walked with full inward integrity, *does in fact* end the cycle of births. The Tirthankara is not theorizing; he is reporting what he sees. Dhanya's name is now sealed in that report.

**6. SIMPLY PUT**

Gautama asked: "How long will Dhanya live as a god, and what will happen after?" — and Mahavira answered: "He will live as a god in Sarvarthasiddha for thirty-three sāgaropamas, and after that he will be born once more as a human in the region of Mahavideha — where he will attain final liberation."

**7. CONTEMPLATE**

If you knew with certainty that one more lifetime would complete your liberation — would you live this present life as a careful preparation, or as just another forgettable detour?

---

### SUTRA 3.A1.S29 — Nikshepa (Closing of Adhyayana 1)

**1. PRAKRIT TEXT**

एवं खलु जंबू ! समणेणं भगवया महावीरेणं जाव संपत्तेणं पढमस्स अज्झयणस्स अयमट्ठे पण्णत्ते ।

।। पढमं अज्झयणं समत्तं ।। ॥3.A1.S29॥

**2. ROMAN TRANSLITERATION**

evaṃ khalu jaṃbū ! samaṇeṇaṃ bhagavayā mahāvīreṇaṃ jāva saṃpatteṇaṃ paḍhamassa ajjhayaṇassa ayamaṭṭhe paṇṇatte |

|| paḍhamaṃ ajjhayaṇaṃ samattaṃ || || 3.A1.S29 ||

**3. LITERAL ENGLISH TRANSLATION**

"Truly so, Jambu! This is the meaning of the first sub-chapter that the liberated Sramana Lord Mahavira has declared." — Thus ends the first sub-chapter.

**4. ANVAYARTHA**

*evaṃ khalu jaṃbū* = "Truly so, O Jambu" | *samaṇeṇaṃ bhagavayā mahāvīreṇaṃ* = by the Sramana Lord Mahavira | *jāva saṃpatteṇaṃ* = up to "the one who has attained (final liberation)" | *paḍhamassa ajjhayaṇassa* = of the first sub-chapter (of the Third Varga) | *ayamaṭṭhe paṇṇatte* = this meaning has been declared | *paḍhamaṃ ajjhayaṇaṃ samattaṃ* = the first sub-chapter is concluded

**5. COMMENTARY**

This is the formal *nikshepa* — the canonical closure-statement that seals every chapter of the *daśā* literature. Sudharma Swami declares to Jambu Swami that the meaning of the first sub-chapter of the Third Varga has been transmitted exactly as Mahavira declared it. The structure of *utkshepa* (opening question) and *nikshepa* (closing seal) frames every adhyayana of the canon, and this brief sutra completes that frame for the long story of Dhanya Kumar.

The canonical compression *jāva saṃpatteṇaṃ* — "up to 'the one who has attained'" — is the standard reverent epithet of Mahavira: *the one who has reached the final goal*. Its repetition at the closing of each chapter functions as a seal of authenticity: the teaching is stamped with the authority of one who has himself reached liberation, not of one who is still a seeker.

The chapter closes here. The reader has now witnessed, in twenty-nine sutras across parts A, B, and C, the entire trajectory of a single soul: from Bhadra Sarthavahi's pious yearning for a son, through Dhanya's birth, his sumptuous youth, his thirty-two royal weddings, his hearing of Mahavira's discourse, his radical renunciation, his four severe vows, his daily practice of one alms-piece taken with no taste-attachment, his wasted body radiant with inner fire, Mahavira's public verdict that he is the foremost ascetic of the entire fourteen-thousand-strong order, King Shrenika's personal veneration, the late-night vigil reflection, the ascent of Vipula mountain, the one-month sallekhana, the supreme equipoise-death, the rise past every cosmic realm to Sarvarthasiddha, and the prophesied liberation in Mahavideha.

That is the arc of one chapter — one of three in this Varga, and one of three Vargas in this scripture. The text now turns to the next sub-chapter, in which the same arc will be told of Sunakshatra Kumar, Dhanya's spiritual brother, in compressed form.

**6. SIMPLY PUT**

The teacher Sudharma seals the first sub-chapter, telling Jambu: "This is the full meaning of the first sub-chapter that Mahavira declared" — and so the long story of Dhanya is formally complete.

**7. CONTEMPLATE**

A whole life can be sealed in a single sentence at the end of a chapter — what sentence would the witness to your life write at the end of yours?

---

## Adhyayana 2 — Sunakshatra Kumar

### SUTRA 3.A2.S1 — Sunakshatra Kumar's Life and Renunciation (Utkshepa, Body, and Tapas)

**1. PRAKRIT TEXT**

उक्खेवओ बिइयस्स ।

एवं खलु जंबू ! तेणं कालेणं तेणं समएणं काकंदी नयरी । जियसत्तू राया । तत्थ णं काकंदीए नयरीए भद्दा णामं सत्थवाही परिवसइ, अड्ढा जाव अपरिभूया । तीसे णं भद्दाए सत्थवाहीए पुत्ते सुणक्खत्ते णामं दारए होत्था अहीणं पंचिंदिय जाव सुरूवे । पंचधाइपरिक्खित्ते, जहा धण्णो तहा जाव उप्पिं पासायवरगए जाव पच्चणुब्भवमाणा विहरइ ।

तेणं कालेणं तेणं समएणं समणस्स भगवओ महावीरस्स समोसरणं । जहा धण्णो तहा सुणक्खत्तो वि निग्गओ । जहा थावच्चापुत्तस्स तहा सुणक्खत्तस्स णिक्खमणं जाव अणगारे जाए ईरियासमिए जाव बंभयारी ।

तए णं से सुणक्खत्ते अणगारे जं चेव दिवसं समणस्स भगवओ महावीरस्स अंतिए मुंडे भवित्ता अगाराओ अणगारियं पव्वइए तं चेव दिवसं, एवं जहेव धण्णो तहेव अभिग्गहं अभिगिण्हइ जाव बिलमिवपण्णग भूएणं अप्पाणेणं आहारं आहारेइ, आहारेत्ता संजमेणं तवसा अप्पाणं भावेमाणे विहरइ । सामी बहिया जणवय-विहारं विहरइ । एक्कारस अंगाइं अहिज्जइ जाव संजमेणं तवसा अप्पाणं भावेमाणे विहरइ । तए णं से सुणक्खत्ते अणगारे तेणं उरालेणं जाव जहा खंदओ । ॥3.A2.S1॥

**2. ROMAN TRANSLITERATION**

ukkhevao biiyassa |

evaṃ khalu jaṃbū ! teṇaṃ kāleṇaṃ teṇaṃ samaeṇaṃ kākaṃdī nayarī | jiyasattū rāyā | tattha ṇaṃ kākaṃdīe nayarīe bhaddā ṇāmaṃ satthavāhī parivasai, aḍḍhā jāva aparibhūyā | tīse ṇaṃ bhaddāe satthavāhīe putte suṇakkhatte ṇāmaṃ dārae hotthā ahīṇaṃ paṃciṃdiya jāva surūve | paṃcadhāiparikkhitte, jahā dhaṇṇo tahā jāva uppiṃ pāsāyavaragae jāva paccaṇubbhavamāṇā viharai |

teṇaṃ kāleṇaṃ teṇaṃ samaeṇaṃ samaṇassa bhagavao mahāvīrassa samosaraṇaṃ | jahā dhaṇṇo tahā suṇakkhatto vi niggao | jahā thāvaccāputtassa tahā suṇakkhattassa ṇikkhamaṇaṃ jāva aṇagāre jāe īriyāsamie jāva baṃbhayārī |

tae ṇaṃ se suṇakkhatte aṇagāre jaṃ ceva divasaṃ samaṇassa bhagavao mahāvīrassa aṃtie muṃḍe bhavittā agārāo aṇagāriyaṃ pavvaie taṃ ceva divasaṃ, evaṃ jaheva dhaṇṇo taheva abhiggahaṃ abhigiṇhai jāva bilamivapaṇṇaga bhūeṇaṃ appāṇeṇaṃ āhāraṃ āhārei, āhārettā saṃjameṇaṃ tavasā appāṇaṃ bhāvemāṇe viharai | sāmī bahiyā jaṇavaya-vihāraṃ viharai | ekkārasa aṃgāiṃ ahijjai jāva saṃjameṇaṃ tavasā appāṇaṃ bhāvemāṇe viharai | tae ṇaṃ se suṇakkhatte aṇagāre teṇaṃ urāleṇaṃ jāva jahā khaṃdao | || 3.A2.S1 ||

**3. LITERAL ENGLISH TRANSLATION**

"The opening of the second sub-chapter." — "Truly so, Jambu! In that age, at that time, there was a city called Kakandi. The king there was Jitashatru. In the city of Kakandi lived a caravan-leader's wife named Bhadra, wealthy — and so on, up to — never disregarded by anyone. Bhadra Sarthavahi had a son named Sunakshatra, a youth perfect in his five senses — and so on — handsome of form. Surrounded by five wet-nurses — as with Dhanya, so also with him — he dwelt in the upper apartments of his finest mansion, enjoying every human pleasure. In that age, at that time, the holy assembly of the Sramana Lord Mahavira gathered. As Dhanya did, so Sunakshatra also went forth (to hear the Lord). As with Thavachhaputra, so the renunciation of Sunakshatra is to be understood — up to — he became a homeless monk, careful in his steps, and a celibate. Then, on the very day Sunakshatra became a shaven-headed monk in the presence of the Sramana Lord Mahavira and renounced the household for the houseless life, on that very day, just as Dhanya had done, he too undertook the great vow — and so on, up to — he eats his food disinterestedly, like a serpent entering its hole; eating thus, he abides while purifying the soul through restraint and austerity. The Lord went forth on tour through the outlying countries. (Sunakshatra) studied the eleven Anga scriptures, abiding while purifying the soul through restraint and austerity. Then the venerable monk Sunakshatra, by that severe (austerity) — and so on, just as with Skandaka."

**4. ANVAYARTHA**

*ukkhevao biiyassa* = the opening (utkshepa) of the second sub-chapter | *evaṃ khalu jaṃbū* = "Truly so, O Jambu" | *teṇaṃ kāleṇaṃ teṇaṃ samaeṇaṃ* = in that age, at that time | *kākaṃdī nayarī* = the city of Kakandi | *jiyasattū rāyā* = King Jitashatru ("conqueror of foes") | *bhaddā ṇāmaṃ satthavāhī* = a caravan-leader's wife named Bhadra (the same Bhadra Sarthavahi who is Dhanya's mother) | *parivasai* = lived | *aḍḍhā* = wealthy | *aparibhūyā* = never overcome / never disregarded | *putte suṇakkhatte ṇāmaṃ dārae* = a son, a youth named Sunakshatra ("good star, auspicious constellation") | *ahīṇaṃ paṃciṃdiya* = whole and complete in his five senses | *surūve* = handsome of form | *paṃcadhāi-parikkhitte* = surrounded by five wet-nurses (the standard royal upbringing) | *jahā dhaṇṇo tahā* = as with Dhanya, so (with him) | *uppiṃ pāsāyavaragae* = on the upper floor of his finest mansion | *paccaṇubbhavamāṇā viharai* = he dwelt enjoying (sensual pleasures) | *samosaraṇaṃ* = the holy gathering of Mahavira | *jahā dhaṇṇo tahā suṇakkhatto vi niggao* = as Dhanya, so Sunakshatra too went forth | *jahā thāvaccāputtassa tahā suṇakkhattassa ṇikkhamaṇaṃ* = the renunciation of Sunakshatra is as that of Thavachhaputra (the famous monk in *Jnatadharmakatha*, fifth chapter, used here as the reference template for the renunciation ceremony) | *aṇagāre jāe* = he became a homeless monk | *īriyāsamie* = careful in walking (one of the five *samitis* — observances of careful conduct) | *baṃbhayārī* = a celibate | *jaṃ ceva divasaṃ* = on the very day | *muṃḍe bhavittā* = having become shaven-headed | *agārāo aṇagāriyaṃ pavvaie* = renounced from the household state to the houseless state | *abhiggahaṃ abhigiṇhai* = he undertakes the great vow (the four severe abhigrahas Dhanya took) | *bilamivapaṇṇaga bhūeṇaṃ appāṇeṇaṃ* = with a soul like a serpent entering its hole | *āhāraṃ āhārei* = takes his food | *saṃjameṇaṃ tavasā appāṇaṃ bhāvemāṇe viharai* = abides while purifying the soul through restraint and austerity | *sāmī bahiyā jaṇavaya-vihāraṃ viharai* = the Lord went forth on tour through the outlying countries | *ekkārasa aṃgāiṃ ahijjai* = he studied the eleven Anga scriptures | *teṇaṃ urāleṇaṃ jāva jahā khaṃdao* = "by that severe (austerity practice) — and so on, just as with Skandaka" — meaning the long body-description of emaciation given for Skandaka (and Dhanya) is to be applied here as well

**5. COMMENTARY**

The second sub-chapter opens with the canonical compression-marker *ukkhevao biiyassa* — "the opening of the second" — a single phrase that stands in for the entire ceremonial preamble (Jambu asks the next question, Sudharma announces the new chapter). The body of the sutra then tells, in compressed form, the entire life of Sunakshatra Kumar — laid out exactly along the template of Dhanya's life, which the previous chapter has just established in full.

The historical setting reveals an important detail: Sunakshatra is *also* a son of Bhadra Sarthavahi. The text names her by her exact title — *bhaddā ṇāmaṃ satthavāhī* — using the same words used of Dhanya's mother in part A. This means that Dhanya and Sunakshatra are biological brothers, sons of the same caravan-leader's wife in Kakandi. The Gujarati commentary makes this point explicitly: "(Sunakshatra) was the son of mother Bhadra and the (real) brother of the venerable monk Dhanya." Two sons of the same mother thus walked the same path of renunciation under the same Tirthankara, both in this very chapter ascending to the same supreme heaven.

The reigning king of Kakandi is named here as Jitashatru — "conqueror of foes," a common royal title in the canonical literature. This is a different city and a different king from those of Dhanya's earlier sutras (where the praise-scene took place under Shrenika in Rajagriha); Kakandi is the home city, and the Mahavira-arrival now is in Kakandi itself.

The compression is dense. *Jahā dhaṇṇo tahā* — "as with Dhanya, so" — folds the upbringing by five wet-nurses, the marriage to thirty-two princesses, the dwelling on the upper floor of the mansion, the awakening at Mahavira's discourse, all into Dhanya's template. *Jahā thāvaccāputtassa tahā suṇakkhattassa ṇikkhamaṇaṃ* — "the renunciation is as that of Thavachhaputra" — uses a *different* template for the actual ordination ceremony: Thavachhaputra is a famous monk whose detailed renunciation-ceremony is recorded in the fifth chapter of the *Jnatadharmakatha Sutra*, and the text directs the reader there for the full procedure. The redactor's instruction is precise: for the upbringing and marriage, use Dhanya's account; for the renunciation rite, use Thavachhaputra's. The Gujarati commentary makes this explicit and recommends that "the reader should study the fifth chapter of the *Jnatadharmakatha Sutra* in order to understand Thavachhaputra; Dhanya's account is already given in this Varga's first sub-chapter."

After ordination, Sunakshatra's life is described as identical to Dhanya's at every point: the same daily one-alms-piece practice, the same disinterested eating "like a serpent entering its hole," the same careful conduct in walking, the same celibacy, the same nine-year-equivalent integration of restraint and austerity. He studies the eleven Anga scriptures — the standard curriculum of the Jain renunciate's intellectual training. And then, the text says, *teṇaṃ urāleṇaṃ jāva jahā khaṃdao* — "by that severe austerity, [his body became wasted] just as with Skandaka." The full body-description of emaciation (the legs like sticks, the spine like a rosary, the eyes like broken pots, the body like fire under ash) is to be transposed onto Sunakshatra in full. The text refuses to repeat what has already been said; it asks the reader to repeat it inwardly.

The deepest lesson of this sutra is that the path is replicable. What Dhanya did, his real brother Sunakshatra also did, in the same household, in the same generation, with the same mother. The compiler does not give us a different story for Sunakshatra because, at the level of soul, the story is the same. Once a being has aligned with right vision, right knowledge, and right conduct, the road is one road — only the name on the cushion changes.

**6. SIMPLY PUT**

In Kakandi city, mother Bhadra had another son — Sunakshatra, Dhanya's real brother — who lived the same wealthy life, heard Mahavira's same discourse, took the same renunciation, kept the same disciplines, ate his food without tasting it, studied the same scriptures, and brought his body to the same wasted, radiant condition.

**7. CONTEMPLATE**

When you see someone close to you walk the spiritual path you long for, do you feel inspired to follow — or threatened that the path now expects something of you?

---

### SUTRA 3.A2.S2 — Sunakshatra's Sallekhana, Ascent to Sarvarthasiddha, and Future Liberation

**1. PRAKRIT TEXT**

तेणं कालेणं तेणं समएणं रायगिहे णयरे । गुणसिलए चेइए । सेणिए राया । सामी समोसढे । परिसा णिग्गया । राया णिग्गओ । धम्मकहा । राया पडिगओ । परिसा पडिगया ।

तए णं तस्स सुणक्खत्तस्स अणगारस्स अण्णया कयाइ पुव्वरत्तावरत्त-कालसमयंसि धम्म-जागरियं सेसं जहा खंदयस्स णवरं बहु वासा परियाओ जाव सव्वट्ठुसिद्धे विमाणे देवत्ताए उववण्णे । तेत्तीसं सागरोवमाइं ठिई जाव महाविदेहे सिज्झिहिइ । ॥3.A2.S2॥

**2. ROMAN TRANSLITERATION**

teṇaṃ kāleṇaṃ teṇaṃ samaeṇaṃ rāyagihe ṇayare | guṇasilae ceie | seṇie rāyā | sāmī samosaḍhe | parisā ṇiggayā | rāyā ṇiggao | dhammakahā | rāyā paḍigao | parisā paḍigayā |

tae ṇaṃ tassa suṇakkhattassa aṇagārassa aṇṇayā kayāi puvvarattāvaratta-kālasamayaṃsi dhamma-jāgariyaṃ sesaṃ jahā khaṃdayassa ṇavaraṃ bahu vāsā pariyāo jāva savvaṭṭhasiddhe vimāṇe devattāe uvavaṇṇe | tettīsaṃ sāgarovamāiṃ ṭhiī jāva mahāvidehe sijjhihii | || 3.A2.S2 ||

**3. LITERAL ENGLISH TRANSLATION**

In that age, at that time, in the city of Rajagriha, at the Gunashilaka sacred grove, King Shrenika reigned. The Lord (Mahavira) arrived. The assembly came forth, the king came forth, the dharma was preached, the king returned, the assembly returned. Then once, in the late hours of the night, while the venerable monk Sunakshatra was keeping the dharma-vigil — the rest is as it was for Skandaka — only that his ascetic tenure was many years. — and so on, up to — he was reborn as a divine being in the Sarvarthasiddha celestial mansion. His lifespan there is thirty-three sāgaropamas — and so on — in Mahavideha he will attain liberation.

**4. ANVAYARTHA**

*teṇaṃ kāleṇaṃ teṇaṃ samaeṇaṃ* = in that age, at that time | *rāyagihe ṇayare* = in the city of Rajagriha | *guṇasilae ceie* = at the Gunashilaka sacred grove | *seṇie rāyā* = King Shrenika | *sāmī samosaḍhe* = the Lord arrived (in holy procession) | *parisā ṇiggayā* = the assembly came forth | *rāyā ṇiggao* = the king came forth | *dhammakahā* = the dharma-discourse | *rāyā paḍigao, parisā paḍigayā* = the king and the assembly returned | *tae ṇaṃ* = then | *aṇṇayā kayāi* = once, at some time | *puvvarattāvaratta-kālasamayaṃsi* = at the late-night, after-midnight hour | *dhamma-jāgariyaṃ* = the dharma-vigil | *sesaṃ jahā khaṃdayassa* = the rest as in (the account of) Skandaka | *ṇavaraṃ* = the only difference | *bahu vāsā pariyāo* = his ascetic tenure was of many years | *jāva* = up to (the canonical compression) | *savvaṭṭhasiddhe vimāṇe devattāe uvavaṇṇe* = he was reborn as a divine being in the Sarvarthasiddha celestial mansion | *tettīsaṃ sāgarovamāiṃ ṭhiī* = his lifespan is thirty-three *sāgaropamas* | *mahāvidehe sijjhihii* = he will attain liberation in Mahavideha

**5. COMMENTARY**

This sutra closes the entire arc of Sunakshatra Kumar in a single dense passage. The redactor uses every device of canonical compression: the setting is given in single-word notations (*Rāyagihe ṇayare, Guṇasilae ceie, Seṇie rāyā, Sāmī samosaḍhe* — "Rajagriha city, Gunashilaka grove, King Shrenika, the Lord arrived"); the assembly's coming and going is given in the bare formula (*parisā ṇiggayā, rāyā ṇiggao, dhammakahā, rāyā paḍigao, parisā paḍigayā*); the night-vigil reflection is given by reference (*sesaṃ jahā khaṃdayassa* — "the rest as in the Skandaka account"); the cosmic ascent is given by the single *jāva*; and the future liberation is sealed in three words: *mahāvidehe sijjhihii*.

The single individuating note is the length of the ascetic tenure: *bahu vāsā pariyāo* — "many years." Where Dhanya's tenure was nine months, Sunakshatra's was many years. The text does not specify the exact count; the Gujarati commentary on the sister-Adhyayanas (3-10) lists it as nine years. ⚠️ The exact number for Sunakshatra is not stated in this sutra itself; "many years" is the only specification, and the nine-year figure given in the next sutra (Adhyayana 3-10) refers to a parallel allocation that may or may not include Sunakshatra. The reader should treat "many years" as the certain reading and "nine years" as the more probable but not uniquely specified figure.

The destination, however, is unambiguous. Sunakshatra reaches Sarvarthasiddha — the same supreme heaven as his elder brother. Both sons of Bhadra Sarthavahi end in the same celestial mansion, with the same lifespan, and the same prophecy of liberation in Mahavideha. The brothers who shared a mother on earth share a heaven in the cosmos and will share the final attainment.

The commentary in the Gujarati edition adds an extended note on the phrase *puvvaratta-avaratta-kāla-samayaṃsi* — "the late-night, after-midnight hour." It identifies this as the canonical hour of dharma-vigil for two reasons: first, because at midnight the external environment is at its most still, the mind becomes one-pointed, mental restlessness subsides, and meditation is most effective — therefore the great souls of the canon (Dhanya, Sunakshatra, and others) characteristically have their decisive inward reflection in that hour; second, because in the *Daśavaikālika Sutra*'s second chūlikā, the *pūrvabhāga* and *paścimabhāga* of the night — the time of going to sleep and the time of waking — are specifically prescribed for the seeker as moments of *dharma-jāgariyā*, in which one contemplates the development of one's virtues and the acknowledgment of one's lapses. The hour of midnight is thus the hour of the soul's clearest seeing, and the canon places its great spiritual decisions there for that reason.

The closing — *mahāvidehe sijjhihii* — completes the second chapter. Sunakshatra, like Dhanya, will end his cycle of births in the Mahavideha region, where Tirthankaras eternally teach. The thirty-three *sāgaropama* lifespan in Sarvarthasiddha will pass; one human birth in Mahavideha will follow; liberation will then be sealed.

**6. SIMPLY PUT**

After many years as a monk, Sunakshatra — like his brother Dhanya — had his decisive inward awakening in the late-night hour, undertook a final fast, died in equanimity, and was reborn in the highest heaven Sarvarthasiddha for thirty-three vast cosmic eras, after which he too will attain final liberation in the Mahavideha region.

**7. CONTEMPLATE**

The path that one walked has been walked again, by his own brother — what does that say about the path, and what does it say about you?

---

## Adhyayana 3-10 — Isidasa and the Eight (Collective)

### SUTRA 3.A3-10.S1 — The Eight Remaining Sub-Chapters Compressed

**1. PRAKRIT TEXT**

एवं सुणक्खत्त गमेणं सेसा वि अट्टु अज्झयणा भाणियव्वा । णवरं आणुपुव्वीए दोण्णि रायगिहे, दोण्णि साकेए, दोण्णि वाणियग्गामे । णवमो हत्थिणा पुरे । दसमो रायगिहे । णवण्हं भद्दाओ जणणीओ, णवण्हं वि बत्तीसओ दाओ । णवण्हं णिक्खमणं थावच्चापुत्तस्स सरिसं । वेहल्लस्स (णिक्खमणं) पिया करेइ । छम्मासा वेहल्लए । णव धण्णे । सेसाणं बहु वासा । मास संलेहणा । सव्वट्टुसिद्धे सव्वे । महाविदेहे सिज्झिस्संति । एवं दस अज्झयणाणि । ॥3.A3-10.S1॥

**2. ROMAN TRANSLITERATION**

evaṃ suṇakkhatta gameṇaṃ sesā vi aṭṭu ajjhayaṇā bhāṇiyavvā | ṇavaraṃ āṇupuvvīe doṇṇi rāyagihe, doṇṇi sākee, doṇṇi vāṇiyaggāme | ṇavamo hatthiṇā pure | dasamo rāyagihe | ṇavaṇhaṃ bhaddāo jaṇaṇīo, ṇavaṇhaṃ vi battīsao dāo | ṇavaṇhaṃ ṇikkhamaṇaṃ thāvaccāputtassa sarisaṃ | vehallassa (ṇikkhamaṇaṃ) piyā karei | chammāsā vehallae | ṇava dhaṇṇe | sesāṇaṃ bahu vāsā | māsa saṃlehaṇā | savvaṭṭhasiddhe savve | mahāvidehe sijjhissaṃti | evaṃ dasa ajjhayaṇāṇi | || 3.A3-10.S1 ||

**3. LITERAL ENGLISH TRANSLATION**

In the same manner as the Sunakshatra account, the remaining eight sub-chapters also are to be told. The only difference is that, in due order: two were of Rajagriha, two of Saketa, two of Vanijyagrama; the ninth was of Hastinapura; the tenth was of Rajagriha. Of (these) nine, the mother was Bhadra; of (these) nine also, the dowry was thirty-two-fold (i.e., thirty-two princesses with thirty-two-fold gifts). The renunciation of (these) nine was like that of Thavachhaputra. The (renunciation-festival) of Vehalla was performed by his father. (The ascetic tenure of) Vehalla was six months. (Of) Dhanya, nine (months). Of the rest, many years. (All had) one-month sallekhana. All (were reborn) in Sarvarthasiddha. All will attain liberation in Mahavideha. Thus the ten sub-chapters (of this Varga).

**4. ANVAYARTHA**

*evaṃ suṇakkhatta gameṇaṃ* = thus, in the same manner as Sunakshatra | *sesā vi aṭṭu ajjhayaṇā bhāṇiyavvā* = the remaining eight sub-chapters also are to be told | *ṇavaraṃ* = the only difference (is) | *āṇupuvvīe* = in due order, in sequence | *doṇṇi rāyagihe* = two (princes) of Rajagriha | *doṇṇi sākee* = two of Saketa (the city of Ayodhya) | *doṇṇi vāṇiyaggāme* = two of Vanijyagrama (a major Magadhan town) | *ṇavamo hatthiṇā pure* = the ninth (was) of Hastinapura | *dasamo rāyagihe* = the tenth (was) of Rajagriha | *ṇavaṇhaṃ bhaddāo jaṇaṇīo* = of the (first) nine, the mothers (were) named Bhadra | *ṇavaṇhaṃ vi battīsao dāo* = of the nine also, the gifts were thirty-two-fold (each married thirty-two princesses, each bringing thirty-two-fold dowry) | *ṇavaṇhaṃ ṇikkhamaṇaṃ thāvaccāputtassa sarisaṃ* = the renunciation of the nine was similar to that of Thavachhaputra | *vehallassa ṇikkhamaṇaṃ piyā karei* = the renunciation-festival of Vehalla was performed by his father | *chammāsā vehallae* = (the ascetic tenure of) Vehalla was six months | *ṇava dhaṇṇe* = (of) Dhanya, nine (months) | *sesāṇaṃ bahu vāsā* = of the rest, many years | *māsa saṃlehaṇā* = a one-month sallekhana | *savvaṭṭhasiddhe savve* = all (were reborn) in Sarvarthasiddha | *mahāvidehe sijjhissaṃti* = (all) will attain liberation in Mahavideha | *evaṃ dasa ajjhayaṇāṇi* = thus, the ten sub-chapters

**5. COMMENTARY**

This single sutra is the great compression of the Third Varga. In it, the entire life-account of *eight* monks — Isidasa, Pellaka, Ramaputta, Chandima, Pedhalaputta, Potilla, Padma, and Vehalla — is folded into the template of Sunakshatra, which was itself folded into the template of Dhanya. The redactor refuses to tell the eight stories separately, because at the level of soul they are the same story.

The text gives only the differentiating coordinates. The eight (counted with Dhanya and Sunakshatra to make ten) are distributed as follows: two each from three cities, then one from a fourth, and one again from the first.

⚠️ The standard reading of the order of distribution, based on the listing of names in the canonical tradition and on the *bhāvārtha* in the Gujarati edition (PDF p. 53), assigns:
- Adhyayana 1: Dhanya — Kakandi
- Adhyayana 2: Sunakshatra — Kakandi
- Adhyayanas 3-4: Isidasa and Pellaka — Saketa (Ayodhya)
- Adhyayanas 5-6: Ramaputta and Chandima — Vanijyagrama
- Adhyayanas 7-8: Pedhalaputta and Potilla — *(allocation here is uncertain in the Gujarati commentary, which acknowledges this)*
- Adhyayana 9: Padma — Hastinapura
- Adhyayana 10: Vehalla — Rajagriha

The Gujarati *vivechan* on PDF p. 53 explicitly notes the ambiguity: *"In this Varga, the description of ten souls is given. Although the mothers of (the first) nine are all said to be named Bhadra, the cities of these ten are different. The first two princes were ordained by their mothers (Bhadra of Kakandi); the tenth (Vehalla) was ordained by his father. ⚠️ The cities and family identities of the ten princes named here cannot be determined with certainty in every case (literally, "no firm decision can be made about whether they were brothers, real or otherwise"). Because of the brevity of the sutra, full clarity does not arise."*

The text does, however, give us several universal certainties:
1. **Mothers**: Of the first nine, every mother was named Bhadra. The repetition of the name Bhadra ("the auspicious one") across nine cities and nine households is striking, but the canonical text accepts the parallel without comment. ⚠️ Some scholars read this as nine separate mothers, each happening to be named Bhadra; others read it as a typological repetition. The source PDF makes no doctrinal claim either way.
2. **Marriages**: All nine were married to thirty-two princesses, each bringing thirty-two-fold gifts — exactly as Dhanya was. The luxury of their pre-renunciation lives was identical.
3. **Renunciation rite**: For the first nine, the ordination ceremony followed the Thavachhaputra template (recorded in *Jnatadharmakatha*, fifth chapter). For the tenth — Vehalla — the rite was performed by his father, not by his mother as it was for Dhanya and the others. The Gujarati commentary highlights this as the singular point of difference.
4. **Ascetic tenure**: Vehalla kept the shortest tenure — six months. Dhanya kept nine months. The rest kept many years (the commentary on the parallel passage gives nine years as the reading for the others).
5. **Sallekhana**: All ten kept the standard one-month *māsa-saṃlehaṇā* — the same length of final fast as the twenty-three of Vargas 1 and 2. This unifies the entire scripture under a single ascetic discipline.
6. **Destination**: All ten were reborn in *Sarvarthasiddha* — every single one, without exception. Where Varga 2 had only five of its thirteen rise to Sarvarthasiddha, Varga 3 has every one of its ten rise there. This Varga is therefore the chapter of the supreme: every soul recorded here is one human birth from final liberation.
7. **Future liberation**: All ten will attain *siddhi* in Mahavideha. *Sijjhissaṃti* is plural, future-definite, no caveats.

The doctrinal weight of this sutra is enormous. It declares that ten great souls — across four cities, born to nine mothers, married into nine households, ordained under various circumstances — walked the same essential path, took the same final fast, ascended to the same supreme heaven, and will reach the same final liberation. The scripture is testifying that the path is *generic* — not bound to any particular city, family, or accident of biography — and that whoever walks it with full integrity reaches the same end.

The closing line — *evaṃ dasa ajjhayaṇāṇi* — "thus, the ten sub-chapters" — completes the body of the Third Varga. The remaining sutras of the Varga are the Nikshepa (formal seal of the Varga) and the Parishesha (closing colophon on the structure of the entire scripture).

**6. SIMPLY PUT**

The remaining eight monks of this chapter — Isidasa, Pellaka, Ramaputta, Chandima, Pedhalaputta, Potilla, Padma, and Vehalla — lived essentially the same life as Sunakshatra and Dhanya: born to mothers named Bhadra, married to thirty-two princesses, ordained under Mahavira, fasted to a one-month death; all ten were reborn in the very highest heaven, and all ten will attain final liberation in the Mahavideha region.

**7. CONTEMPLATE**

Ten different souls in four different cities walked one identical path to the same end — what excuse does your particular biography offer for not walking it?

---

### SUTRA 3.A3-10.S2 — Nikshepa (Closing of the Third Varga)

**1. PRAKRIT TEXT**

एवं खलु जंबू ! समणेणं भगवया महावीरेणं आइगरेणं जाव सिद्धिगइणामधेयं ठाणं संपत्तेणं अणुत्तरोववाइयदसाणं तच्चस्स वग्गस्स अयमट्ठे पण्णत्ते । ॥3.A3-10.S2॥

**2. ROMAN TRANSLITERATION**

evaṃ khalu jaṃbū ! samaṇeṇaṃ bhagavayā mahāvīreṇaṃ āigareṇaṃ jāva siddhigaiṇāmadheyaṃ ṭhāṇaṃ saṃpatteṇaṃ aṇuttarovavāiyadasāṇaṃ taccassa vaggassa ayamaṭṭhe paṇṇatte | || 3.A3-10.S2 ||

**3. LITERAL ENGLISH TRANSLATION**

"Truly so, Jambu! This is the meaning of the third sub-Varga of the Anuttaropapātika Daśā that has been declared by the Sramana Lord Mahavira — the originator of the dharma, the one who has fully reached the station bearing the name of Siddha-gati."

**4. ANVAYARTHA**

*evaṃ khalu jaṃbū* = "Truly so, O Jambu" | *samaṇeṇaṃ bhagavayā mahāvīreṇaṃ* = by the Sramana Lord Mahavira | *āigareṇaṃ* = the originator (of the present dharma-tradition; literally "the one who has made the beginning") | *jāva* = up to (the canonical compression covering all the standard epithets) | *siddhigai-ṇāma-dheyaṃ ṭhāṇaṃ saṃpatteṇaṃ* = the one who has reached the station bearing the name of *siddhi-gati* (the goal of the liberated, the destination called "Siddha-hood") | *aṇuttarovavāiyadasāṇaṃ* = of the Anuttaropapātika Daśā | *taccassa vaggassa* = of the third sub-Varga | *ayamaṭṭhe paṇṇatte* = this meaning has been declared

**5. COMMENTARY**

The Nikshepa here is fuller than the standard one. Where Adhyayana 1's closing was a brief one-line seal (*evaṃ khalu jaṃbū... ayamaṭṭhe paṇṇatte*), the closing of the entire Third Varga uses an expanded epithet: *āigareṇaṃ jāva siddhigai-ṇāma-dheyaṃ ṭhāṇaṃ saṃpatteṇaṃ* — "the originator of the dharma, [up to] the one who has reached the station bearing the name of Siddha-gati."

This longer formula is the full canonical praise-phrase used at the closing of major sections. *Āigara* — "the originator" — declares Mahavira as the one who initiated the present dharma-tradition; in the Jain understanding, every Tirthankara *re-establishes* the eternal dharma in his own age, and *āigara* is the technical term for that re-establishment. The intervening *jāva* compresses the standard epithets that follow: *Tīrthaṅkara* ("ford-maker, builder of the crossing"), *svayaṃ-saṃbuddha* ("self-awakened"), *puruṣottama* ("supreme person"), *puruṣa-siṃha* ("lion among persons"), *puruṣa-varapuṇḍarīka* ("lotus among persons"), *puruṣa-vara-gandhahasti* ("perfumed elephant among persons"), *abhayaṃkara* ("giver of fearlessness"), *cakṣur-da* ("giver of vision"), *mārga-da* ("giver of the path"), *śaraṇa-da* ("giver of refuge"), *jīva-da* ("giver of life-knowledge"), *bodhi-da* ("giver of enlightenment"), *dharma-da* ("giver of dharma"), *dharma-deśaka* ("teacher of dharma"), *dharma-nāyaka* ("leader of dharma"), *dharma-sārathi* ("charioteer of dharma"), *dharma-vara-cāturanta-cakravartin* ("supreme four-edged dharma-emperor"), and so on through the standard litany. *Siddhi-gati-nāma-dheyaṃ ṭhāṇaṃ saṃpatte* — "the one who has reached the station bearing the name of Siddha-gati" — closes the litany; it declares that Mahavira, having walked his own path to the end, has reached the very *siddhi-gati* — the destination of the liberated — which all souls in this scripture are described as approaching.

The Gujarati commentary at this point makes the doctrinal observation explicit: by listing all of Mahavira's epithets at the closing of the entire Varga, the redactor is putting the reader in the position of Jambu — the disciple receiving the teaching — and asking him to feel the full weight of the source from which the teaching has come. *"This formula generates faith and devotion in the reader; it transforms reading into receiving."* The longer the praise-phrase at the seal, the deeper the implicit invitation to receive what has been transmitted.

The third Varga is now formally closed. The thirty-three souls of the entire Anuttaropapātika Daśā — ten in Varga 1, thirteen in Varga 2, and ten in Varga 3 — have all been recorded. All thirty-three reached one of the five Anuttara heavens; all thirty-three will attain final liberation in Mahavideha. The full register of one of the Jain canon's most luminous chapters has been transmitted.

**6. SIMPLY PUT**

The teacher closes the third sub-chapter, telling Jambu: "This is the meaning of the third sub-chapter of the Anuttaropapātika Daśā, declared by Lord Mahavira — the founder of the dharma, who himself has reached the goal of liberation."

**7. CONTEMPLATE**

When you receive a teaching whose source has himself reached the end of the path — does the teaching feel different to you than one received from a fellow seeker still on the way?

---

### SUTRA 3.A3-10.S3 — Parishesha (Closing Colophon on the Structure of the Scripture)

**1. PRAKRIT TEXT**

अणुत्तरोववाइयदसाणं एगो सुयक्खंधो । तिण्णि वग्गा । तिसु चेव दिवसेसु उद्दिसिज्जंति । तत्थ पढमे वग्गे दस उद्देसगा । बिइए वग्गे तेरस उद्देसगा । तइए वग्गे दस उद्देसगा । तओ सुयखंधो समुद्दिसइ, तओ अणुण्णविज्जइ, दोसु दिवसेसु । ॥3.A3-10.S3॥

**2. ROMAN TRANSLITERATION**

aṇuttarovavāiyadasāṇaṃ ego suyakkhaṃdho | tiṇṇi vaggā | tisu ceva divasesu uddisijjaṃti | tattha paḍhame vagge dasa uddesagā | biie vagge terasa uddesagā | taie vagge dasa uddesagā | tao suyakhaṃdho samuddisai, tao aṇuṇṇavijjai, dosu divasesu | || 3.A3-10.S3 ||

**3. LITERAL ENGLISH TRANSLATION**

The Anuttaropapātika Daśā has one *śruta-skandha* (book-section). It has three *vargas* (sub-Vargas, divisions). The teaching is delivered in three days. The first sub-Varga has ten *uddeśas* (recitation-units, lessons). The second has thirteen. The third has ten. After this, the entire *śruta-skandha* is comprehensively recited, and then permission is given (to the student to teach the next scripture); these last two acts are performed across two days.

**4. ANVAYARTHA**

*aṇuttarovavāiyadasāṇaṃ* = of the Anuttaropapātika Daśā | *ego suyakkhaṃdho* = (it has) one *śruta-skandha* (one composite book-section) | *tiṇṇi vaggā* = three *vargas* (sub-Vargas) | *tisu ceva divasesu uddisijjaṃti* = (the three sub-Vargas) are taught/recited across three days (one Varga per day) | *tattha paḍhame vagge dasa uddesagā* = of these, the first sub-Varga has ten *uddeśas* (recitation-units, divisional lessons) | *biie vagge terasa uddesagā* = the second has thirteen *uddeśas* | *taie vagge dasa uddesagā* = the third has ten *uddeśas* | *tao suyakhaṃdho samuddisai* = then the entire *śruta-skandha* is comprehensively recited (the *samuddeśa* — the full recitation-review) | *tao aṇuṇṇavijjai* = then permission is given (the *anujñā* — the formal authorization passing from teacher to student to teach this scripture, or to take up the next) | *dosu divasesu* = (these last two activities — *samuddeśa* and *anujñā* — take place) on two (further) days

**5. COMMENTARY**

This sutra is the *parishesha* — the structural colophon. It is not narrative; it is a teaching-protocol. It tells the student of the canon how this scripture is to be transmitted in the traditional Jain pedagogical method.

The numbers given here add up. The Anuttaropapātika Daśā is one *śruta-skandha* — one unified scripture. Within it are three *vargas* — the divisions we have been calling "sub-Vargas." Each sub-Varga is taught on a single day, in one continuous oral session. So the basic teaching takes three days. Within each day's *varga*, the material is broken into *uddeśas* — recitation-units. Varga 1 has ten *uddeśas* (corresponding to the ten princes — Jali through Abhaya); Varga 2 has thirteen *uddeśas* (corresponding to the thirteen princes — Dirghasena through Punyasena); Varga 3 has ten *uddeśas* (corresponding to the ten monks of Kakandi and the other cities — Dhanya through Vehalla). The sum is thirty-three *uddeśas* — the canonical count of thirty-three souls.

After the three teaching-days, two more days are added. On the fourth day, the *samuddeśa* — the comprehensive recitation-review — is performed: the entire *śruta-skandha* is recited from start to finish, all thirty-three *uddeśas* together, in one continuous flow, as a check on memory and integration. On the fifth day, the *anujñā* — the formal authorization — is given: the teacher places his hand on the student's head and authorizes him to teach this scripture to others, or to move on to the next scripture in the curriculum.

The five-day teaching-protocol is itself a discipline. It tells us that this scripture was not meant to be read at random or absorbed in fragments; it was meant to be received in three full sessions of focused listening, then reviewed in one full session, then sealed by the teacher's authorization. The reader who reads the printed Gujarati edition or this English translation is, in effect, telescoping into a moment what the tradition asked to be unfolded across five days. The Gujarati *vivechan* makes the point gently: this five-day method preserves the depth of the transmission and the integrity of the student's capacity to hold it.

The *parishesha* also confirms, beyond any further doubt, the structure of the scripture: ten + thirteen + ten = thirty-three. This count, given here in the closing sutra, is the same count given in the opening sutra of Varga 1 (where Jambu first asks Sudharma about the structure of the ninth Anga). The scripture opens and closes on the same architectural number. Every soul accounted for; every sub-Varga's unit count attested.

The Gujarati editor closes the *vivechan* with a beautiful summary line: *"It must be studied with full attention to receive complete knowledge of this matter; for in this Anga the seeker hears Lord Mahavira's discourse, the arising of detachment, the festival of ordination, the supreme grade of austerity, the wasting of the body, the dharma-vigil, the spirit of the final fast, ascent to Sarvarthasiddha after that fast, future birth in Mahavideha, the attainment of Siddhi — all these subjects are taught in compressed form."*

The colophon line that follows in the printed PDF — *|| varga-3 / 3 thī 10 saṃpūrṇa ||* and *|| anuttaropapātika sūtra saṃpūrṇa ||* — declares the third sub-Varga (sub-chapters 3 through 10) complete, and the entire Anuttaropapātika Sutra complete.

**6. SIMPLY PUT**

This entire scripture has one book, three parts, and thirty-three lessons in total — taught traditionally over three days, then reviewed on a fourth, with the teacher's blessing given on the fifth — and now the whole scripture, all thirty-three lives of those who reached the highest heavens, has been fully transmitted.

**7. CONTEMPLATE**

The masters built a five-day rhythm to receive this teaching well; in your own life, what rhythm would let a great teaching settle into you instead of skim over you?

---

|| वर्ग-३ / ३ थी १० संपूर्ण ||
|| End of Varga 3 / Sub-chapters 3 through 10 ||
|| अणुत्तरोववाइय सूत्र संपूर्ण ||
|| End of the Anuttaropapātika Sutra ||

---

**Translator's Note on Uncertainties Flagged in Part C of Chapter 3:**

- The exact ascetic tenure of Sunakshatra Kumar is given in the source as *bahu vāsā* ("many years") in his own sutra (3.A2.S2); the figure of nine years given by some readings is taken from the parallel passage covering Adhyayanas 3-10 and is not strictly attested for Sunakshatra individually. ⚠️
- The city-and-mother allocation of the eight monks of Adhyayanas 3-10 (Isidasa, Pellaka, Ramaputta, Chandima, Pedhalaputta, Potilla, Padma, Vehalla) is given by the source only in coordinates — two each from Saketa, two from Vanijyagrama, one from Hastinapura, one from Rajagriha — without naming which monk lived in which city. The pairing offered in the commentary above follows the most common scholarly reading but is not uniquely fixed by the source. The Gujarati *vivechan* explicitly acknowledges this ambiguity. ⚠️
- The reading "of the first nine, the mothers were Bhadra" (*ṇavaṇhaṃ bhaddāo jaṇaṇīo*) is given in the source without comment on whether nine separate mothers each happened to be named Bhadra or whether this is a typological repetition; the source PDF makes no doctrinal claim either way. ⚠️
- The reference *jahā khaṃdao* in Sutra 3.A1.S23 and again in 3.A2.S2 points to the body-description of the monk Skandaka in the Bhagavati Sutra (second *shataka*), which is to be read across to the present passage by the canonical method of *atidesha* (reference by analogy). The full Skandaka description is not reproduced here; the reader is to consult the Bhagavati for it.
- The reference *jahā thāvaccāputtassa* in Sutra 3.A2.S1 points to the renunciation-account of Thavachhaputra in the *Jnatadharmakatha Sutra*, fifth chapter; the renunciation-rite of Sunakshatra (and of the first nine of Adhyayanas 3-10) follows that template, not the template of Dhanya whose mother personally arranged his ordination festival.

Jai Jinendra 🙏
